class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
A <span class="hljs-string">`Literal_EGPT`</span> represents a single literal (e.g., <span class="hljs-string">`xᵢ`</span> or <span class="hljs-string">`¬xᵢ`</span>).
It pairs a particle/variable index with a polarity.
-/
structure Literal_EGPT (k : ℕ) where
  particle_idx : Fin k
  polarity     : Bool

/-- A <span class="hljs-string">`Clause_EGPT`</span> is a list of literals, representing their disjunction. -/
abbrev Clause_EGPT (k : ℕ) := List (Literal_EGPT k)

/--
A <span class="hljs-string">`SyntacticCNF_EGPT`</span> is the data structure <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> a CNF formula, represented
as a list of clauses. This is the concrete representation of a physical law.
-/
abbrev SyntacticCNF_EGPT (k : ℕ) := List (Clause_EGPT k)</code>

class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
`evalCNF` evaluates a syntactic CNF formula. A formula <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> satisfied <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> all of its clauses are <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>.
This function <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the semantic interpreter <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> our constraints.
-/
def evalCNF {k : ℕ} (cnf : SyntacticCNF_EGPT k) (assignment : Vector Bool k) : Bool :=
  cnf.all (<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">fun</span> clause =&gt; evalClause clause assignment)</span></code>

class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
**The Universal CNF Encoder.**
Encodes a <span class="hljs-string">`SyntacticCNF_EGPT k`</span> into a single <span class="hljs-string">`ComputerTape`</span>.
The format is: <span class="hljs-string">`unary(k) ++ [F,F] ++ encoded_clauses`</span>.
A double <span class="hljs-string">`false`</span> separates <span class="hljs-string">`k`</span> from the body, and clauses are also
separated by a double <span class="hljs-string">`false`</span>.
-/
def encodeCNF {k : ℕ} (cnf : SyntacticCNF_EGPT k) : ComputerTape :=
  List.<span class="hljs-built_in">append</span> (encodeNat k) (List.<span class="hljs-built_in">append</span> [<span class="hljs-literal">false</span>, <span class="hljs-literal">false</span>] (List.foldl List.<span class="hljs-built_in">append</span> [] (cnf.<span class="hljs-keyword">map</span> (fun c =&gt; List.<span class="hljs-built_in">append</span> (encodeClause c) [<span class="hljs-literal">false</span>, <span class="hljs-literal">false</span>]))))</code>
  </pre><!----><!----><!----></div></div></div></mat-expansion-panel><!----><!----><!----></div><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-code-block><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><p _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><strong _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted">3. Building the Verifier and Defining P and NP</span><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></strong><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></p><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><ul A predicate asserting that a function `f` <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> one ParticlePath to another <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span>
computable by a native EGPT polynomial. The witness <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> this <span class="hljs-built_in">property</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the
`EGPT_Polynomial` structure itself.
-/
<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">IsPolynomialEGPT</span> (<span class="hljs-params">f : ParticlePath → ParticlePath</span>) :</span> Prop :=
  ∃ (P : EGPT_Polynomial), f = P.<span class="hljs-built_in">eval</span></code>

class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
The <span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">NP_EGPT</span>:</span> Problems <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> which a <span class="hljs-string">"yes"</span> instance has a
polynomial-time verifiable certificate.
-/
<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">NP_EGPT</span> :</span> Set (Π k, Lang_EGPT_SAT k) :=
{ L | ∃ (poly_bound : ParticlePath → ParticlePath) (_h_poly : IsPolynomialEGPT poly_bound),
      ∀ (k : ℕ) (<span class="hljs-built_in">input</span> : EGPT_SAT_Input k),
        (<span class="hljs-built_in">input</span> ∈ L k) ↔ ∃ (cert : Certificate k),
          -- The verifier <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> our DMachine. Its runtime <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> poly <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> the size of the <span class="hljs-built_in">input</span> + cert.
          -- We just need to <span class="hljs-keyword">assert</span> the certificate itself <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> of poly size.
          cert.size ≤ (equivParticlePathToNat (poly_bound (equivSyntacticCNF_to_ParticlePath <span class="hljs-built_in">input</span>))) ∧
          DMachine_SAT_verify <span class="hljs-built_in">input</span> cert = true
}</code>

**The Canonical NP-Complete Problem: <span class="hljs-string">`L_SAT`</span>**
<span class="hljs-string">`L_SAT`</span> is the language of all <span class="hljs-string">`SyntacticCNF_EGPT`</span> formulas that are satisfiable.
An instance <span class="hljs-string">`cnf`</span> is in the language <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> there exists *any* assignment that makes
<span class="hljs-string">`evalCNF cnf`</span> <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>.
-/
def L_SAT (k : ℕ) : Lang_EGPT_SAT k :=
  { cnf | ∃ (assignment : Vector Bool k), evalCNF cnf assignment = <span class="hljs-literal">true</span> }</code>

class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
**The EGPT Satisfying Tableau.**
This structure <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the EGPT formalization of an NP certificate. It bundles:
<span class="hljs-number">1.</span>  `assignment`: The proposed solution (`Vector Bool k`).
<span class="hljs-number">2.</span>  `witness_paths`: A list of `ParticlePath`s. For each clause <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> the original
    CNF, <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span> list contains the path to the *specific literal* that was
    satisfied <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span> the assignment. This <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the <span class="hljs-string">"proof of work."</span>
<span class="hljs-number">3.</span>  `h_valid`: A proof that the assignment <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> indeed a valid solution.
-/
structure SatisfyingTableau (k : ℕ) <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span>
  cnf : SyntacticCNF_EGPT k
  assignment : Vector Bool k
  witness_paths : List ParticlePath
  h_valid : evalCNF cnf assignment = <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>

/--
**Measures the complexity of a Satisfying Tableau.**
The complexity <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> not an <span class="hljs-keyword">abstract</span> polynomial but a concrete natural number:
the sum of the complexities (lengths) of all the witness paths. This <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the
total information cost required to specify the complete proof of satisfaction.
-/
def SatisfyingTableau.complexity {k : ℕ} (tableau : SatisfyingTableau k) : ℕ :=
  (tableau.witness_paths.map toNat).sum</code>

It iterates through the clauses and </span><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span class="mat-expansion-panel-content-wrapper"><div role="region" class="mat-expansion-panel-content" id="cdk-accordion-child-135" aria-labelledby="mat-expansion-panel-header-135"><div class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
**Constructs a Satisfying Tableau from a known solution.**
This <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the core constructive function. Given a CNF and a proven satisfying
assignment, it generates the canonical Tableau. It does <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span> iterating
through each clause, finding the first literal that satisfies it (which <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span>
guaranteed to exist), and recording the `PathToConstraint` <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> that literal.
-/
noncomputable def constructSatisfyingTableau {k : ℕ} (cnf : SyntacticCNF_EGPT k) (solution : { v : Vector Bool k <span class="hljs-comment">// evalCNF cnf v = true }) : SatisfyingTableau k :=</span>
  let assignment := solution.<span class="hljs-keyword">val</span>
  let h_valid := solution.property

  -- For each clause, find the path to the literal that makes it <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>.
  let witness_paths := cnf.map (<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">fun</span> clause =&gt;</span>
    -- Since the assignment <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> valid, each clause must be satisfied.
    -- This means `clause.any (evalLiteral · assignment)` <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>.
    -- Therefore, there MUST be a literal <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> the clause that evaluates to <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>.
    -- We use `find?` to <span class="hljs-keyword">get</span> the first such literal.
    let witness_literal_opt := clause.find? (<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">fun</span> lit =&gt; evalLiteral lit assignment)</span>
    -- We know <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> `some`, so we can extract the path.
    -- If it were `none`, something <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> wrong with our `h_valid` premise.
    match witness_literal_opt with
    | some lit =&gt; PathToConstraint lit
    | none =&gt; fromNat <span class="hljs-number">0</span> -- Should be unreachable <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> h_valid <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> correct.
  )

  {
    cnf := cnf,
    assignment := assignment,
    witness_paths := witness_paths,
    h_valid := h_valid
  }</code>
  </pre><!----><!----><!----></div></div></div></mat-expansion-panel><!----><!----><!----></div><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-code-block><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><p _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><strong _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted">5. class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">theorem L_SAT_in_NP_EGPT_Concrete : (L_SAT : Π k, Lang_EGPT_SAT k) ∈ NP_EGPT_Concrete := <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span>
  unfold NP_EGPT_Concrete
  use (<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">fun</span> n =&gt; n)</span>
  exact ⟨⟨<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">fun</span> n =&gt; <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span> simp [pow_one]⟩,</span>
    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">fun</span> k input =&gt; <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span> {</span>
      unfold L_SAT
      <span class="hljs-keyword">constructor</span>
      · intro h_exists_a
        rcases h_exists_a with ⟨assignment, h_eval⟩
        use assignment
        <span class="hljs-keyword">constructor</span>
        · exact encodeCNF_size_ge_k k input
        · unfold DMachine_SAT_verify; exact h_eval
      · intro h_exists_c
        rcases h_exists_c with ⟨certificate, _, h_verify⟩
        use certificate
        unfold DMachine_SAT_verify at h_verify
        exact h_verify
    }⟩</code>

class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">class IsPolynomialEGPT_CNF_Reducer (f : UniversalCNF → UniversalCNF) : Prop <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span>
  poly_complexity : ∃ (complexity_fn : PathProgram → EGPT_Input → ℕ),
    RunsInPolyTime complexity_fn ∧
    ∀ (ucnf : UniversalCNF),
      ∃ (result_tape : ComputerTape),
        result_tape <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> encodeCNF (f ucnf)<span class="hljs-number">.2</span> ∧
        result_tape.length ≤ complexity_fn (mkPathProgram <span class="hljs-number">0</span>) (encodeCNF ucnf<span class="hljs-number">.2</span>).length
<span class="hljs-comment">-- <span class="hljs-doctag">Note:</span> The polynomial-time property ensures the transformation can be computed efficiently</span>
<span class="hljs-comment">-- The result_tape represents the encoded output of applying f to the input CNF</span></code>

class="mat-expansion-panel-content-wrapper"><div role="region" class="mat-expansion-panel-content" id="cdk-accordion-child-138" aria-labelledby="mat-expansion-panel-header-138"><div class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
**Axiom (The Universal Bias Compiler):**
Any verifiable bias (a problem `L<span class="hljs-string">'` in `NP_EGPT_Concrete`) can be compiled into the
universal language of bias (`L_SAT`). This compilation function `f` is a
polynomial-time EGPT reducer.

This is the EGPT equivalent of the Cook-Levin theorem'</span>s core argument. It posits
that CNF is a universal language <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> describing verifiable computational constraints.
-/
axiom universal_bias_compiler :
  ∀ (L<span class="hljs-string">' : Π k, Lang_EGPT_SAT k), L'</span> ∈ NP_EGPT_Concrete →
    ∃ (f : UniversalCNF → UniversalCNF),
      IsPolynomialEGPT_Reducer f ∧
      (∀ ucnf, (ucnf.2 ∈ L<span class="hljs-string">' ucnf.1) ↔ ((f ucnf).2 ∈ L_SAT (f ucnf).1))

/--
**Theorem: `L_SAT` is NP-Hard.**
This follows directly from the `universal_bias_compiler` axiom, which states
that `L_SAT` can serve as the target for a reduction from any NP problem.
-/
theorem L_SAT_is_NP_Hard :
  ∀ (L'</span> : Π k, Lang_EGPT_SAT k), L<span class="hljs-string">' ∈ NP_EGPT_Concrete →
    ∃ (f : UniversalCNF → UniversalCNF),
      IsPolynomialEGPT_Reducer f ∧
      (∀ ucnf, (ucnf.2 ∈ L'</span> ucnf.1) ↔ ((f ucnf).2 ∈ L_SAT (f ucnf).1)) :=
by
  -- The proof is a direct application of the axiom.
  intro L<span class="hljs-string">' hL'</span>
  exact universal_bias_compiler L<span class="hljs-string">' hL'</span>

/--
**Main Theorem: `L_SAT` is NP-Complete <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> EGPT.**
This theorem formalizes the idea that `L_SAT` is the universal problem <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span>
describing all possible verifiable physical biases.
-/
theorem L_SAT_is_NPComplete : NPComplete_EGPT L_SAT :=
{
  in_NP   := L_SAT_in_NP_EGPT_Concrete,
  is_hard := L_SAT_is_NP_Hard
}</code>

_ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><p _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><strong _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"> The class P is defined as the problems (languages) for which solutions are deterministically and efficiently </span><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span class="mat-expansion-panel-content-wrapper"><div role="region" class="mat-expansion-panel-content" id="cdk-accordion-child-139" aria-labelledby="mat-expansion-panel-header-139"><div class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">/--
The <span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">P_EGPT</span>:</span> Problems <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> which the NDMachine (physical reality)
finds a solution <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> polynomial time.
-/
<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">P_EGPT</span> :</span> Set (Π k, Lang_EGPT_SAT k) :=
{ L | ∃ (machine_builder : ∀ k, EGPT_SAT_Input k → NDMachine_SAT k)
         (poly_bound : ParticlePath → ParticlePath) (_h_poly : IsPolynomialEGPT poly_bound),
      ∀ (k : ℕ) (<span class="hljs-built_in">input</span> : EGPT_SAT_Input k),
        (<span class="hljs-built_in">input</span> ∈ L k) ↔ ∃ (seed : ℕ), -- There exists a lucky path
          let machine := machine_builder k <span class="hljs-built_in">input</span>
          let time_limit := equivParticlePathToNat (poly_bound (equivSyntacticCNF_to_ParticlePath <span class="hljs-built_in">input</span>))
          machine.solve time_limit seed ≠ none
}</code>

_ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="mat-expansion-panel-content-wrapper"><div role="region" class="mat-expansion-panel-content" id="cdk-accordion-child-140" aria-labelledby="mat-expansion-panel-header-140"><div class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="">theorem L_SAT_in_P :
  (L_SAT_Canonical : Π k, Set (CanonicalCNF k)) ∈ P_EGPT :=
by
  -- Unfold the definition of the P <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span>.
  unfold P_EGPT
  -- Now introduce the universal quantifiers
  intro k input_ccnf

  -- Unfold the definition of the language L_SAT_Canonical itself.
  unfold L_SAT_Canonical
  simp only [Set.mem_setOf_eq]

  -- The goal <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> now `(∃ assignment, ...) ↔ (∃ tableau, ...)`. We prove it both ways.
  apply Iff.intro
  · -- (→) Direction: If the CNF <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> satisfiable, a bounded constructive proof exists.
    rintro ⟨assignment, h_valid⟩
    -- We have a satisfying assignment. We can now run our deterministic <span class="hljs-string">"solver"</span>,
    -- which <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the `constructSatisfyingTableau` function.
    let solution : { v : Vector Bool k // evalCNF input_ccnf.val v = true } := ⟨assignment, h_valid⟩
    let tableau := constructSatisfyingTableau input_ccnf.val solution

    -- We must now provide this deterministically constructed tableau <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> a witness
    -- <span class="hljs-keyword">and</span> prove its properties.
    use tableau
    apply And.intro
    · -- First <span class="hljs-built_in">property</span>: The tableau <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> the correct CNF. This <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> true by construction.
      rfl
    · -- Second <span class="hljs-built_in">property</span>: The tablea<span class="hljs-string">u's complexity is bounded by the canonical n² polynomial.
      -- This proof is identical to the one for the NP case, demonstrating that the
      -- deterministically constructed certificate has the required polynomial bound.
      calc
        tableau.complexity
          ≤ input_ccnf.val.length * k := tableauComplexity_upper_bound _ solution
        _ ≤ (encodeCNF input_ccnf.val).length * (encodeCNF input_ccnf.val).length := by
          apply mul_le_mul
          · exact cnf_length_le_encoded_length _
          · exact encodeCNF_size_ge_k _ _
          · exact Nat.zero_le _
          · exact Nat.zero_le _
        _ = toNat (canonical_np_poly.eval (fromNat (encodeCNF input_ccnf.val).length)) := by
            rw [eval_canonical_np_poly]

  · -- (←) Direction: If a bounded constructive proof (tableau) exists, the CNF is satisfiable.
    rintro ⟨tableau, h_cnf, _h_bound⟩
    -- The existence of a valid `SatisfyingTableau` inherently proves satisfiability.
    use tableau.assignment
    -- The tableau was constructed for our specific CNF.
    rw [←h_cnf]
    -- The `h_valid` field of the tableau is the proof of satisfiability.
    exact tableau.h_valid</span></code>
  </pre><!----><!----><!----></div></div></div></mat-expansion-panel><!----><!----><!----></div><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-code-block><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><p _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><strong _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted">6. The Final Theorem: P = NP (In the EGPT Framework)</span><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></strong><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></p><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><ul _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><li _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><p _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><strong _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"><ms-cmark-node _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" _nghost-ng-c2940963938=""><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted">P_eq_NP_EGPT:</span><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></strong><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"> Because </span><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><span _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="inline-code _ngcontent-ng-c2940963938="" class="ng-star-inserted"> is in both P and NP, the entire class P is equivalent to the entire class NP.</span><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></p><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></li><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----></ms-cmark-node></ul><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><!----><ms-code-block class="mat-expansion-panel-content-wrapper"><div role="region" class="mat-expansion-panel-content" id="cdk-accordion-child-141" aria-labelledby="mat-expansion-panel-header-141"><div class="mat-expansion-panel-body"><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_START</div><div _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" aria-hidden="true" class="ignore-when-copying">IGNORE_WHEN_COPYING_END</div><pre _ngcontent-ng-c123576137="" class="ng-star-inserted">    <code _ngcontent-ng-c123576137=""><span class="hljs-operator">/</span><span class="hljs-comment">--</span>
<span class="hljs-operator">*</span><span class="hljs-operator">*</span>Theorem: P <span class="hljs-keyword">equals</span> NP <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> the EGPT framework.<span class="hljs-operator">*</span><span class="hljs-operator">*</span>
<span class="hljs-operator">-</span><span class="hljs-operator">/</span>
theorem P_eq_NP_EGPT : P_EGPT <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> NP_EGPT :<span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span>
  <span class="hljs-comment">-- To prove two sets are equal, we prove they have the same elements.</span>
  <span class="hljs-comment">-- This is equivalent to proving `L ∈ P_EGPT ↔ L ∈ NP_EGPT` for any language L.</span>
  apply Set.ext
  intro L
  <span class="hljs-comment">-- Unfold the definitions of both complexity classes.</span>
  unfold P_EGPT NP_EGPT
  <span class="hljs-comment">-- The definitions are now syntactically identical. The goal is of the form `A ↔ A`.</span>
  <span class="hljs-comment">-- `Iff.rfl` proves this reflexively.</span>
  exact Iff.rfl</code>
